Warming Her Pearls (by Carol Ann Duffy)

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Next to my own skin, her pearls. My mistress⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;bids me wear them, warm them, until evening⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;when I'll brush her hair. At six, I place them⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;round her cool, white throat. All day I think of her,⟯</span>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;resting in the Yellow Room, contemplating silk⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;or taffeta, which gown tonight? She fans herself⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;whilst I work willingly, my slow heat entering⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;each pearl. Slack on my neck, her rope.⟯</span>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;She's beautiful. I dream about her⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;in my attic bed; picture her dancing⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;with tall men, puzzled by my faint, persistent scent⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;beneath her French perfume, her milky stones.⟯</span>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;I dust her shoulders with a rabbit's foot,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;watch the soft blush seep through her skin⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;like an indolent sigh. In her looking-glass⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;my red lips part as though I want to speak.⟯</span>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;Full moon. Her carriage brings her home. I see⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;her every movement in my head.... Undressing,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;taking off her jewels, her slim hand reaching⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;for the case, slipping naked into bed, the way⟯</span>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;she always does.... And I lie here awake,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:22;s:all;knowing the pearls are cooling even now⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:23;s:all;in the room where my mistress sleeps. All night⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:24;s:all;I feel their absence and I burn.⟯</span>
</blockquote>



To be or not to be

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;To be, or not to be, that is the question:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;Whether 'tis nobler in the mind to suffer⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;The slings and arrows of outrageous fortune,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;Or to take Arms against a Sea of troubles,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;And by opposing end them: to die, to sleep⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;No more; and by a sleep, to say we end⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;The heart-ache, and the thousand natural shocks⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;That Flesh is heir to? 'Tis a consummation⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;Devoutly to be wished. To die, to sleep,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;To sleep, perchance to Dream; aye, there's the rub,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;For in that sleep of death, what dreams may come,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;When we have shuffled off this mortal coil,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;Must give us pause. There's the respect⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;That makes Calamity of so long life:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;For who would bear the Whips and Scorns of time,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;The Oppressor's wrong, the proud man's Contumely,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;The pangs of dispised Love, the Law’s delay,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;The insolence of Office, and the spurns⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;That patient merit of th'unworthy takes,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;When he himself might his Quietus make⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;With a bare Bodkin? Who would Fardels bear, [F: these Fardels]⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:22;s:all;To grunt and sweat under a weary life,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:23;s:all;But that the dread of something after death,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:24;s:all;The undiscovered country, from whose bourn⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:25;s:all;No traveller returns, puzzles the will,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:26;s:all;And makes us rather bear those ills we have,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:27;s:all;Than fly to others that we know not of?⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:28;s:all;Thus conscience does make cowards of us all,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:29;s:all;And thus the native hue of Resolution⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:30;s:all;Is sicklied o'er, with the pale cast of Thought,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:31;s:all;And enterprises of great pitch and moment, [F: pith]⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:32;s:all;With this regard their Currents turn awry, [F: away]⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:33;s:all;And lose the name of Action.⟯</span>
</blockquote>

Thou knowst the mask of night...

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Thou know’st the mask of night is on my face,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;Else would a maiden blush bepaint my cheek⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;For that which thou hast heard me speak tonight.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;Fain would I dwell on form. Fain, fain deny⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;What I have spoke. But farewell compliment!⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;Dost thou love me? I know thou wilt say “ay,”⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;And I will take thy word. Yet if thou swear’st⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;Thou mayst prove false. At lovers' perjuries,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;They say, Jove laughs. O gentle Romeo,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;If thou dost love, pronounce it faithfully.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;Or if thou think’st I am too quickly won,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;I’ll frown and be perverse and say thee nay,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;So thou wilt woo. But else, not for the world.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;In truth, fair Montague, I am too fond,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;And therefore thou mayst think my 'havior light.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;But trust me, gentleman, I’ll prove more true⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;Than those that have more coying to be strange.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;I should have been more strange, I must confess,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;But that thou overheard’st, ere I was 'ware,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;My true love’s passion. Therefore pardon me,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;105And not impute this yielding to light love,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:22;s:all;Which the dark night hath so discovered.⟯</span>
</blockquote>

The Serenity Prayer

<span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;God, grant me the serenity to accept the things I cannot change,⟯</span>

The Merchant of Venice: Act III, Scene 1, Shylock Monologue

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;To bait fish withal: if it will feed nothing else,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;it will feed my revenge. He hath disgraced me, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;and hindered me half a million; laughed at my losses,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;mocked at my gains, scorned my nation, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;thwarted my bargains, cooled my friends, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;heated mine enemies; and what's his reason? ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;I am a Jew. Hath not a Jew eyes? ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;hath not a Jew hands, organs, dimensions, senses, affections, passions? ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;fed with the same food, hurt with the same weapons, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;subject to the same diseases, healed by the same means,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;warmed and cooled by the same winter and summer, as⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;a Christian is? If you prick us, do we not bleed?⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;if you tickle us, do we not laugh? ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;if you poison us, do we not die? ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;and if you wrong us, shall we not revenge? ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;If we are like you in the rest, we will resemble you in that. ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;If a Jew wrong a Christian, what is his humility? Revenge. ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;If a Christian wrong a Jew, what should his sufferance be, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;by Christian example? Why, revenge. ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;The villany you teach me, I will execute, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;and it shall go hard but I will better the instruction.⟯</span>
</blockquote>

The Merchant of Venice, Act 1 Scene 3, Shylocks Monologue

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Signior Antonio, many a time and oft⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;In the Rialto you have rated me⟯</span>

Símon Bolivar's conclusion about the americas

Simon Bolivars Letter near the end of his life:
<ol>
  <li>⟮c:1;s:all;America is ungovernable.⟯</li>
  <li>⟮c:2;s:all;He who serves revolution plows the sea.⟯</li>
  <li>⟮c:3;s:all;The only thing one can do in America is emigrate.⟯</li>
  <li>⟮c:4;s:all;This country will first fall into the hands of the unbridled crowd and then pass imperceptibly to tyrants of all colors and races.⟯</li>
  <li>⟮c:5;s:all;Devoured by all crimes and extinguished by ferocity, the Europeans will not even deign to conquer us.⟯</li>
  <li>⟮c:6;s:all;If it is possible for one part of the world to return to primitive chaos, it is America.⟯</li>
</ol>

Speech: “Tomorrow, and tomorrow, and tomorrow
 (from Macbeth, spoken by Macbeth)
 
 <blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Tomorrow, and tomorrow, and tomorrow,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;Creeps in this petty pace from day to day,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;To the last syllable of recorded time;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;And all our yesterdays have lighted fools⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;The way to dusty death. Out, out, brief candle!⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;Life's but a walking shadow, a poor player,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;That struts and frets his hour upon the stage,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;And then is heard no more. It is a tale⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;Told by an idiot, full of sound and fury,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;Signifying nothing.⟯</span>
</blockquote>

Once more unto the breach!

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Once more unto the breach, dear friends, once more;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;Or close the wall up with our English dead.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;In peace there's nothing so becomes a man⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;As modest stillness and humility:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;But when the blast of war blows in our ears,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;Then imitate the action of the tiger;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;Stiffen the sinews, summon up the blood,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;Disguise fair nature with hard-favour'd rage;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;Then lend the eye a terrible aspect;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;Let pry through the portage of the head⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;Like the brass cannon; let the brow o'erwhelm it⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;As fearfully as doth a galled rock⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;O'erhang and jutty his confounded base,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;Swill'd with the wild and wasteful ocean.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;Now set the teeth and stretch the nostril wide,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;Hold hard the breath and bend up every spirit⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;To his full height. On, on, you noblest English.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;Whose blood is fet from fathers of war-proof!⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;Fathers that, like so many Alexanders,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;Have in these parts from morn till even fought⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;And sheathed their swords for lack of argument:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:22;s:all;Dishonour not your mothers; now attest⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:23;s:all;That those whom you call'd fathers did beget you.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:24;s:all;Be copy now to men of grosser blood,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:25;s:all;And teach them how to war. And you, good yeoman,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:26;s:all;Whose limbs were made in England, show us here⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:27;s:all;The mettle of your pasture; let us swear⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:28;s:all;That you are worth your breeding; which I doubt not;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:29;s:all;For there is none of you so mean and base,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:30;s:all;That hath not noble lustre in your eyes.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:31;s:all;I see you stand like greyhounds in the slips,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:32;s:all;Straining upon the start. The game's afoot:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:33;s:all;Follow your spirit, and upon this charge⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:34;s:all;Cry 'God for Harry, England, and Saint George!'⟯</span>
</blockquote>

Hamilton - Non-Stop (extract)

<span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Alexander joins forces with James Madison and John Jay to write a series⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;of essays defending the new United States Constitution,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;entitled The Federalist Papers.⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;The plan was to write a total of twenty-five essays,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;the work divided evenly among the three men. In the end,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;they wrote eighty-five essays,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;in the span of six months. John Jay got sick after writing five.⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;James Madison wrote twenty-nine. Hamilton wrote the other fifty-one!⟯</span>

John Chivington, 1864, about indians

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;I have come to kill Indians,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;and believe it is right and honorable to use⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;any means under God's heaven to kill Indians.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;Kill and scalp all, big and little; nits make lice!⟯</span>

⟮c:3;It is too rash, too unadvised, too sudden,⟯ ⟮c:2;Too like the lightning, which doth cease to be⟯ ⟮c:1;Ere one can say “It lightens.”⟯ 

Helen of Troy Does Countertop Dancing (by Margaret Atwood)

<blockquote> 
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;The world is full of women⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;who'd tell me I should be ashamed of myself⟯</span>

Gettysburg Address (1863)

<p>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Four score and seven years ago our fathers brought forth on this continent,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;a new nation, conceived in Liberty⟯</span>, 
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;and dedicated to the proposition that all men are created equal.⟯</span>
  </p>
  <p>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;Now we are engaged in a great civil war,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;testing whether that nation,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;or any nation so conceived and so dedicated,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;can long endure.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;We are met on a great battle-field of that war.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;We have come to dedicate a portion of that field, as a final resting place⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;for those who here gave their lives that that nation might live.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;It is altogether fitting and proper that we should do this. ⟯</span>
  </p>
  <p>
  <span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;But, in a larger sense,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;we can not dedicate—⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;we can not consecrate—⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;we can not hallow—this ground. ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;The brave men, living and dead, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;who struggled here, have consecrated it, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;far above our poor power to add or detract. ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;The world will little note, nor long remember what we say here, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;but it can never forget what they did here. ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;It is for us, the living, rather, ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:22;s:all;to be dedicated here to the unfinished work ⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:23;s:all;which they who fought here have thus far so nobly advanced.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:24;s:all;It is rather for us to be here dedicated to the great task remaining before us—⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:25;s:all;that from these honored dead we take increased devotion⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:26;s:all;to that cause for which they gave the last full measure of devotion—⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:27;s:all;that we here highly resolve that these dead shall not have died in vain—⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:28;s:all;that this nation, under God,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:29;s:all;shall have a new birth of freedom—⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:30;s:all;and that government of the people,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:31;s:all;by the people,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:32;s:all;for the people,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:33;s:all;shall not perish from the earth.⟯</span>
  </p>
<span class="cloze-dump">{{c1::}}{{c2::}}{{c3::}}{{c4::}}{{c5::}}{{c6::}}{{c7::}}{{c8::}}{{c9::}}{{c10::}}{{c11::}}{{c12::}}{{c13::}}{{c14::}}{{c15::}}{{c16::}}{{c17::}}{{c18::}}{{c19::}}{{c20::}}{{c21::}}{{c22::}}{{c23::}}{{c24::}}{{c25::}}{{c26::}}{{c27::}}{{c28::}}{{c29::}}{{c30::}}{{c31::}}{{c32::}}{{c33::}}</span><br><div class="sub">

Friends, Romans, Countrymen

<blockquote>
  <span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Friends, Romans, countrymen, lend me your ears;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;I come to bury Caesar, not to praise him.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;The evil that men do lives after them;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;The good is oft interred with their bones;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;So let it be with Caesar. The noble Brutus⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;Hath told you Caesar was ambitious:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;If it were so, it was a grievous fault,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;And grievously hath Caesar answer’d it.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;Here, under leave of Brutus and the rest–⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;For Brutus is an honourable man;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;So are they all, all honourable men–⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;Come I to speak in Caesar’s funeral.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;He was my friend, faithful and just to me:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;But Brutus says he was ambitious;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;And Brutus is an honourable man.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:16;s:all;He hath brought many captives home to Rome⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:17;s:all;Whose ransoms did the general coffers fill:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:18;s:all;Did this in Caesar seem ambitious?⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:19;s:all;When that the poor have cried, Caesar hath wept:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:20;s:all;Ambition should be made of sterner stuff:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:21;s:all;Yet Brutus says he was ambitious;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:22;s:all;And Brutus is an honourable man.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:23;s:all;You all did see that on the Lupercal⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:24;s:all;I thrice presented him a kingly crown,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:25;s:all;Which he did thrice refuse: was this ambition?⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:26;s:all;Yet Brutus says he was ambitious;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:27;s:all;And, sure, he is an honourable man.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:28;s:all;I speak not to disprove what Brutus spoke,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:29;s:all;But here I am to speak what I do know.⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:30;s:all;You all did love him once, not without cause:⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:31;s:all;What cause withholds you then, to mourn for him?⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:32;s:all;O judgment! thou art fled to brutish beasts,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:33;s:all;And men have lost their reason. Bear with me;⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:34;s:all;My heart is in the coffin there with Caesar,⟯</span>
  <span class="line">⟮c:35;s:all;And I must pause till it come back to me.⟯</span>
</blockquote>

Do Not Go Gentle into that Good Night

<span class="line">⟮c:1;s:all;Do not go gentle into that good night⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:2;s:all;Old age should burn and rave at close of day;⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:3;s:all;Rage, rage against the dying of the light.⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:4;s:all;Though wise men at their end know dark is right,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:5;s:all;Because their words had forked no lightning they⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:6;s:all;Do not go gentle into that good night.⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:7;s:all;Good men, the last wave by, crying how bright⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:8;s:all;Their frail deeds might have danced in a green bay,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:9;s:all;Rage, rage against the dying of the light.⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:10;s:all;Wild men who caught and sang the sun in flight,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:11;s:all;And learn, too late, they grieved it on its way,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:12;s:all;Do not go gentle into that good night.⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:13;s:all;Grave men, near death, who see with blinding sight⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:14;s:all;Blind eyes could blaze like meteors and be gay,⟯</span>
<span class="line">⟮c:15;s:all;Rage, rage against the dying of the light.⟯</span>

## breath

⟮c:1;four-stage breathing techniques⟯ (roughly equivalent to ⟮c:2;pranayama⟯) consists of the steps ⟮s:gb;((c:3;::Breathe in⟯ ⟮s:gb;((c:4;::Hold⟯ ⟮s:gb;((c:5;::Breathe out⟯ ⟮s:gb;((c:6;::hold⟯.))))))))  
Often, ⟮c:7;the four steps of four-stage breathing/pranayama are the same length⟯, in that case, it is often called ⟮c:8;box/square breath⟯. Commonly, each step is held for ⟮c:9;4-5⟯s.
